     <p>
      <b>
       Better Place
      </b>
      was a
      <a href="/wiki/Venture_capital" title="Venture capital">
       venture-backed
      </a>
      international company that developed and sold battery-charging and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battery_swapping" title="Battery swapping">
       battery-switching
      </a>
      services for
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">
       electric cars
      </a>
      . It was formally based in
      <a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto,_California" title="Palo Alto, California">
       Palo Alto, California
      </a>
      , but the bulk of its planning and operations were steered from
      <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
       Israel
      </a>
      , where both its founder
      <a href="/wiki/Shai_Agassi" title="Shai Agassi">
       Shai Agassi
      </a>
      and its chief investors resided.
     </p>
     <p>
      The company opened its first functional charging station the first week of December 2008 at Cinema City in Pi-Glilot near
      <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">
       Tel Aviv
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
       Israel
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first customer deliveries of
      <a href="/wiki/Renault_Fluence_Z.E." title="Renault Fluence Z.E.">
       Renault Fluence Z.E.
      </a>
      electric cars enabled with battery switching technology began in Israel in the second quarter of 2012,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deliveries2012_2-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Deliveries2012-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and at peak in mid September 2012, there were 21 operational battery-swap stations open to the public in Israel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BWSet12_3-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BWSet12-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Better Place filed for bankruptcy in Israel in May 2013. The company's financial difficulties were caused by mismanagement, wasteful efforts to establish toeholds and run pilots in too many countries, the high investment required to develop the charging and swapping infrastructure, and a market penetration far lower than originally predicted by Shai Agassi. Less than 1,000 Fluence Z.E. cars were deployed in Israel and around 400 units in Denmark, after spending about
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$850
      </span>
      million in private capital.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT052613_5-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT052613-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JPost052613_6-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-JPost052613-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After two failed post-bankruptcy acquisition attempts,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ingrid_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Ingrid-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Globes082013_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Globes082013-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-successfail_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-successfail-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the bankruptcy receivers sold off the remaining assets in November 2013 to
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Grngy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Grngy (page does not exist)">
       Grngy
      </a>
      for only $450,000.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gnrgy1_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-gnrgy1-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Launch">
       Launch
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Launch">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The company was publicly launched on October 29, 2007, as Project Better Place, by
      <a href="/wiki/Shai_Agassi" title="Shai Agassi">
       Shai Agassi
      </a>
      , the company's founder and CEO at the time. According to Agassi, his vision was inspired by a question asked by
      <a href="/wiki/Klaus_Schwab" title="Klaus Schwab">
       Klaus Schwab
      </a>
      at the 2005
      <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">
       World Economic Forum
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Davos" title="Davos">
       Davos
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
       Switzerland
      </a>
      : "How do you make the world a
      <i>
       better place
      </i>
      by 2020?"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of January 2011 it had raised $700 million, and about a third was spent in setting up the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battery_exchange_station#Battery_swapping" title="Battery exchange station">
       battery switch stations
      </a>
      . Also, several countries and states had offered
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tax_breaks" title="Tax breaks">
       tax breaks
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT0409_12-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT0409-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Better Place announced deployment of
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_network" title="Electric vehicle network">
       electric vehicle networks
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
       Israel
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">
       Denmark
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">
       Hawaii
      </a>
      in 2008 and 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT0409_12-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT0409-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The company planned to deploy the infrastructure on a country-by-country basis, and said it was in talks with more than 25 additional regions around the world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">
       Australia
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">
       Ontario
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">
       Oregon
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
       California
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      also announced deployment of Better Place electric car networks.
     </p>
     <p>
      In January 2008, Better Place announced a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memorandum_of_Understanding" title="Memorandum of Understanding">
       Memorandum of Understanding
      </a>
      (MOU) with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renault-Nissan" title="Renault-Nissan">
       Renault-Nissan
      </a>
      to build the world's first Electric Recharge Grid Operator (ERGO) model for Israel. Under the agreement, Better Place would build the electric recharge grid, and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renault-Nissan" title="Renault-Nissan">
       Renault-Nissan
      </a>
      would provide the
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">
       electric vehicles
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Bankruptcy">
       Bankruptcy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Bankruptcy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D7%AA%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%94%D7%97%D7%9C%D7%A4%D7%AA_%D7%A1%D7%95%D7%9C%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%AA_%D7%A7%D7%A6%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%9F.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/%D7%AA%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%94%D7%97%D7%9C%D7%A4%D7%AA_%D7%A1%D7%95%D7%9C%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%AA_%D7%A7%D7%A6%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%9F.JPG/220px-%D7%AA%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%94%D7%97%D7%9C%D7%A4%D7%AA_%D7%A1%D7%95%D7%9C%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%AA_%D7%A7%D7%A6%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%9F.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/%D7%AA%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%94%D7%97%D7%9C%D7%A4%D7%AA_%D7%A1%D7%95%D7%9C%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%AA_%D7%A7%D7%A6%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%9F.JPG/330px-%D7%AA%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%94%D7%97%D7%9C%D7%A4%D7%AA_%D7%A1%D7%95%D7%9C%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%AA_%D7%A7%D7%A6%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%9F.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/%D7%AA%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%94%D7%97%D7%9C%D7%A4%D7%AA_%D7%A1%D7%95%D7%9C%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%AA_%D7%A7%D7%A6%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%9F.JPG/440px-%D7%AA%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%94%D7%97%D7%9C%D7%A4%D7%AA_%D7%A1%D7%95%D7%9C%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%AA_%D7%A7%D7%A6%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%9F.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D7%AA%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%94%D7%97%D7%9C%D7%A4%D7%AA_%D7%A1%D7%95%D7%9C%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%AA_%D7%A7%D7%A6%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%9F.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A shut-down battery swap station in Israel.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In early October 2012, Agassi resigned from his role as worldwide Better Place CEO, and was replaced by
      <a href="/wiki/Evan_Thornley" title="Evan Thornley">
       Evan Thornley
      </a>
      , CEO of Better Place-Australia. Agassi briefly remained on the company board, but a week later he resigned from that position as well. A few days after Thornley's appointment, Better Place asked its investors for a round of emergency funding, totalling about $100 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On October 29, 2012,
      <a href="/wiki/Ynet" title="Ynet">
       Ynet
      </a>
      reported that Better Place would that week lay off 150 to 200 of its 400-person staff in Israel as it sought financing to combat its cash-flow problems.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In late January 2013, Thornley was fired by Chairman Idan Ofer, and Dan Cohen was named acting CEO by the board.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As a consequence of the financial problems, the Australian rollout was put on hold, as the company decided to concentrate on its two existing markets.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Austonhold_25-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Austonhold-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, on 26 May 2013, Better Place filed for bankruptcy in Israel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Following the decision of the Board of Directors of the global company, Better Place Danmark A/S also decided to initiate bankruptcy proceedings on the same date.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPDenmark01_27-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BPDenmark01-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPDenmark02_28-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BPDenmark02-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The company's financial difficulties were caused by the high investment required to develop the charging and swapping infrastructure, about
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$850
      </span>
      million in private capital, and market penetration significantly lower than originally predicted by Shai Agassi, who expected 100,000 cars on Israeli roads by 2010. Less than 1,000 Fluence Z.E. cars were deployed in Israel and around 400 cars in Denmark.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT052613_5-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT052613-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JPost052613_6-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-JPost052613-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Under Better Place's business model, the company owned the Fluence Z.E. batteries, so the court liquidator would have to decide what to do with customers who do not have ownership of the battery and risk being left with a useless car.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-bankruptcy_acquisition_attempts_and_liquidation">
       Post-bankruptcy acquisition attempts and liquidation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Post-bankruptcy acquisition attempts and liquidation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In July 2013 an attempt to acquire Better Place was made by the Sunrise group that comprised entrepreneur Yosef Abramowitz and the
      <a class="external text" href="http://www.goelectric.org.il/" rel="nofollow">
       Association for the Advancement of Electric Transportation in Israel
      </a>
      . Court filings showed that the acquisition would be worth 18 million Israeli shekels (
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$5 million
      </span>
      ) for Better Places assets in Israel, and 25 million Israeli shekels (
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$7 million
      </span>
      ) for its intellectual property, held by Better Place Switzerland. The deal was canceled by the court after the Sunrise group failed to make the first agreed payment of 3.52 million shekels (
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$976,300
      </span>
      ), even after an extension.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Globes082013_8-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Globes082013-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In August 2013 the Central District Court ruled that Better Place Israel would be sold to Success Assets Ltd., owned by
      <a href="/wiki/Tsahi_Merkur" title="Tsahi Merkur">
       Tsahi Merkur
      </a>
      , for 11 million shekels (
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$3
      </span>
      million). To effect the acquisition, Mekur was to sign a personal guarantee within seven days for the full amount of the acquisition, and a personal guarantee for a letter of indemnification covering the guarantees made by Better Place Israel's subsidiaries to the Ministry of Transport. Within 21 days, Merkur was to deposit with the company's special managers an opinion on a property on which a commitment to register a lien of up to 5 million shekels would be placed. By 30 September 2013 he was to make a payment of 2 million shekels.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Globes082013_8-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Globes082013-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 17 October 2013 the deal was canceled after Success Assets failed to make the required payments.
     </p>
     <p>
      In November 2013 the court-appointed receivers decided to sell the remaining assets of Better Place in parts and liquidate the business.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Business_model">
       Business model
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Business model">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_the_battery_swap_concept">
       History of the battery swap concept
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History of the battery swap concept">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_electric_vehicle" title="History of the electric vehicle">
       History of the electric vehicle
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Steam_car" title="Steam car">
       steam car
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">
       internal combustion engine
      </a>
      automobile, and the
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">
       electric car
      </a>
      emerged as the main competing technologies in the late 1890s until the 1920s. The concept of exchangeable battery service was first proposed as early as 1896 in order to overcome the limited operating range of electric cars and trucks.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HistEV_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HistEV-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The concept was first put into practice by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hartford_Electric_Light_Company" title="Hartford Electric Light Company">
       Hartford Electric Light Company
      </a>
      through the GeVeCo battery service and was initially available for electric trucks. The vehicle owner purchased the vehicle from General Vehicle Company (GeVeCo, a subsidiary of the General Electric Company) without a battery and the electricity was purchased from Hartford Electric through an exchangeable battery. The owner paid a variable per-mile charge and a monthly service fee to cover maintenance and storage of the truck. Both vehicles and batteries were modified to facilitate a fast battery exchange. The service was provided between 1910 to 1924 and during that period vehicles using it covered more than 6 million miles. Beginning in 1917 a similar service was operated in
      <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">
       Chicago
      </a>
      for owners of
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Milburn_Wagon_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Milburn Wagon Company (page does not exist)">
       Milburn Light Electric
      </a>
      cars who also could buy the vehicle without the batteries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HistEV_31-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HistEV-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Electric
      <a href="/wiki/Forklift_truck#History" title="Forklift truck">
       forklifts
      </a>
      have used battery swapping since at least 1946
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-backbone_32-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-backbone-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and a rapid battery replacement system was implemented to help maintain 50 electric buses at the
      <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">
       2008 Summer Olympics
      </a>
      in China.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Better_Place_business_model">
       Better Place business model
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Better Place business model">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Better Place implemented a
      <a href="/wiki/Business_model" title="Business model">
       business model
      </a>
      wherein customers entered into
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subscription" title="Subscription">
       subscriptions
      </a>
      to purchase driving distance similar to the mobile telephone industry from which customers contract for minutes of airtime. The initial cost of an electric vehicle might also have been subsidized by the ongoing per-distance revenue contract just as mobile handset purchases are subsidized by per-minute mobile service contracts. Better Place's goal was to enable electric cars to sell for $5,000 less than the price of the average gasoline car sold in the United States,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.cheatsheet.com_35-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-www.cheatsheet.com-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbc.msn.com_36-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-msnbc.msn.com-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      or the impact of electric cars would be minimal. For example, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prius" title="Prius">
       Prius
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">
       hybrid
      </a>
      had been sold for 13 years at a price of $4,000 more than other gasoline cars and had captured less than 2% of the world wide car market.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-euractiv.com_37-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-euractiv.com-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Better Place approach was to enable manufacturing and sales of different electric cars separately from their standardized batteries
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBS_Morning_News_38-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CBS_Morning_News-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in the same way that petrol cars are sold separately from their fuel. Petrol is not purchased upfront, but is bought a few times a month when the fuel tank needs filling. Similarly, the Better Place monthly payment would cover electric "fuel" costs including battery, daily charging and battery swaps. Better Place was to allow customers to pay incrementally for battery costs including electric power, battery life, degradation, warranty problems, maintenance, capital cost, quality, technology advancement and anything else related to the battery. The per-distance fees would cover
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_battery#Leasing" title="Electric vehicle battery">
       battery pack leasing
      </a>
      , charging and swap infrastructure, purchasing
      <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_energy" title="Sustainable energy">
       sustainable electricity
      </a>
      , profits, and the cost of investor capital.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Agassi_TED_talk_39-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Agassi_TED_talk-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      All battery problems would be handled by Better Place which would then bundle the costs and bill their customers monthly for providing all the infrastructure.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Better Place electric car charging infrastructure network was based on a
      <a href="/wiki/Smart_grid" title="Smart grid">
       smart grid
      </a>
      software platform using
      <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">
       Intel
      </a>
      Atom
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Processors" title="Processors">
       processors
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microsoft_dot-net" title="Microsoft dot-net">
       Microsoft .NET
      </a>
      software, or comparable vendors. This platform was first of its kind in the world and was to enable Better Place to manage the charging of hundreds of thousands of electric cars simultaneously by automatically time-shifting recharging away from peak demand hours of the day, preventing overload of the
      <a href="/wiki/Electrical_grid" title="Electrical grid">
       electrical grid
      </a>
      of the host country.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Better Place would be able to provide electricity for millions of electric cars without adding a single electricity generator or transmission line by using smart software that oversaw and managed the recharging of electric cars connected with Better Place.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Better Place encouraged governments to mandate the use of international standards and open access to recharge across
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_network" title="Electric vehicle network">
       charging networks
      </a>
      to facilitate competing networks.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Agassi_CNBC_42-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Agassi_CNBC-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Standardization efforts such as
      <a href="/wiki/SAE_J1772" title="SAE J1772">
       SAE J1772
      </a>
      , however, had not yet yielded global consensus as of August 2009
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      . Better Place displayed Charge Spot charging stations that used a connector with the same pin layout as SAE J1772-2009 but housed in a non-standard, triangular plug.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-triangle_plug_43-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-triangle_plug-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They also displayed a wall mounted charging station using
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VDE-AR-E_2623-2-2" title="VDE-AR-E 2623-2-2">
       IEC 62196 Type 2
      </a>
      receptacle .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BP_IEC_62196_receptacle_44-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BP_IEC_62196_receptacle-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RWE_2009-04-20_45-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-RWE_2009-04-20-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Battery pack switching outside of Better Place's network was not to be allowed. Better Place said it had pre-sold enough contracts to make its first deployed network in Israel profitable at launch.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_sources">
       Energy sources
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Energy sources">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Agassi stated that the company's plan was to have the network's
      <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">
       electricity
      </a>
      generated entirely by
      <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">
       renewable energy
      </a>
      from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_array" title="Solar array">
       solar arrays
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Wind_farm" title="Wind farm">
       wind farms
      </a>
      if necessary,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT0409_12-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT0409-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      thus invalidating the "long-smokestack" accusation leveled against electric vehicles which rely on the nonrenewable sources of the electricity.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2012)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      However, achieving the 100% renewable energy goal would have depended on the local electric grid's energy sources.
     </p>
     <p>
      In Israel, where the first Better Place deployment took place, the electric grid is based mostly on fossil fuels, rendering the renewable energy vision practically impossible in the short term.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cars_and_batteries">
       Cars and batteries
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Cars and batteries">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BetterPlaceEVsCharging.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/BetterPlaceEVsCharging.JPG/220px-BetterPlaceEVsCharging.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/BetterPlaceEVsCharging.JPG/330px-BetterPlaceEVsCharging.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/BetterPlaceEVsCharging.JPG/440px-BetterPlaceEVsCharging.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BetterPlaceEVsCharging.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Prototype modified
        <a href="/wiki/Renault_Laguna" title="Renault Laguna">
         Renault Laguna
        </a>
        EVs charging at the Better Place visitor centre in
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ramat_Hasharon" title="Ramat Hasharon">
         Ramat Hasharon
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
         Israel
        </a>
        , north of
        <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">
         Tel Aviv
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nissan_erogue.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="531" data-file-width="800" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Nissan_erogue.jpg/220px-Nissan_erogue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Nissan_erogue.jpg/330px-Nissan_erogue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Nissan_erogue.jpg/440px-Nissan_erogue.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nissan_erogue.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Rogue" title="Nissan Rogue">
         Nissan eRogue
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">
         Hawaii
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The first prototype car was the
      <a href="/wiki/Renault_Laguna" title="Renault Laguna">
       Renault Laguna
      </a>
      with a battery instead of a fuel tank and an electric motor instead of an internal combustion engine.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roth_Wired_50-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Roth_Wired-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_battery" title="Electric vehicle battery">
       battery for electric vehicles
      </a>
      was a
      <a href="/wiki/Lithium_iron_phosphate_battery" title="Lithium iron phosphate battery">
       Lithium iron phosphate
      </a>
      ion device.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The range of the car running on just one battery was from about 160 kilometres (99mi)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      to 190 kilometres (120mi).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      By replacing the battery at a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battery_exchange_station#Battery_swapping" title="Battery exchange station">
       battery switch station
      </a>
      , the range between longer
      <a href="/wiki/Charging_station" title="Charging station">
       charging
      </a>
      stops was to be limited only by the geographical distribution of the battery-swapping infrastructure.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roth_Wired_50-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Roth_Wired-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The second demo car was the Nissan eRogue, an electric car based on the
      <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Rogue" title="Nissan Rogue">
       Renault-Nissan Rogue
      </a>
      , half way between a sedan and an SUV in size.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Renault_Fluence_Z.E." title="Renault Fluence Z.E.">
       Renault Fluence Z.E.
      </a>
      was announced at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Motor_Show" title="Frankfurt Motor Show">
       Frankfurt Motor Show
      </a>
      on September 15, 2009 as the first electric car to be available on the Better Place network using a switchable battery.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Shai Agassi said that EVs had to be priced at $5,000 less than the price of the average gasoline car to be successful.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbc.msn.com_36-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-msnbc.msn.com-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In April 2010 Renault announced that sales of the Fluence Z.E. were scheduled for 2011 in
      <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
       Israel
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">
       Denmark
      </a>
      and the rest of Europe.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC0410_56-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-GCC0410-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In August 2010 Better Place announced a non-binding order of 100,000 Renault Fluence ZE
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and four months later Better Place claimed to have sold 70,000 cars from that order, a year away from the public launch of its network.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Disputed statement">
         <span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (January 2012)">
          dubious
         </span>
        </a>
        <span class="metadata">
         
         <a href="/wiki/Talk:Better_Place#where_are_the_sales_figures.3F" title="Talk:Better Place">
          discuss
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The floor-mounted battery packs in these electric cars were designed to be changed out robotically in less than two minutes, which was quicker than the average petroleum refuel, allowing for battery-swap services like those proposed by Better Place and Tesla Motors.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Better Place expected battery packs to cost between US 4 and 5 per mile over their life,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Agassi.2C_Dec_28_2008_60-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Agassi.2C_Dec_28_2008-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      provide the cars with a 160km (99mi) range per charge, perform for 2000 recharge cycles, and last for 8 years.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BP.2C_batteries_61-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BP.2C_batteries-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Battery-switching_stations">
       Battery-switching stations
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Battery-switching stations">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      With areas around cities covered with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battery_swapping" title="Battery swapping">
       battery switching stations
      </a>
      , also called battery-swap stations, drivers would potentially have
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">
       electric cars
      </a>
      with an unlimited driving range for long distance trips.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The QuickDrop battery switch system would enable
      <a href="/wiki/Renault_Fluence_Z.E." title="Renault Fluence Z.E.">
       Renault Fluence Z.E.
      </a>
      's battery, the only vehicle deployed in the Better Place network, to be swapped in approximately three minutes at dedicated battery exchange stations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The actual robotic battery-switching operation took about five minutes in the deployed stations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      While each exchange station would cost $500,000,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-station500k_66-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-station500k-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The then CEO of Better Place, Shai Agassi, said that cost would be half the price of a typical petroleum fuelling station.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Better_Place_Charging_Station_IMG_6670.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2100" data-file-width="2800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Better_Place_Charging_Station_IMG_6670.jpg/220px-Better_Place_Charging_Station_IMG_6670.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Better_Place_Charging_Station_IMG_6670.jpg/330px-Better_Place_Charging_Station_IMG_6670.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Better_Place_Charging_Station_IMG_6670.jpg/440px-Better_Place_Charging_Station_IMG_6670.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Better_Place_Charging_Station_IMG_6670.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Better Place's battery switching Station in Israel
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In order to access the battery switch station, Better Place customers would have to swipe their membership card. The remaining process was fully automated, similar to going through a
      <a href="/wiki/Car_wash" title="Car wash">
       car wash
      </a>
      , so the driver never had to leave the car. In Better Place's demonstration battery switch stations, a robotic arm removed the depleted battery and replaced it with a full one.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC0611_68-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-GCC0611-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During 2010, Better Place operated a demonstration battery switch station in Tokyo allowing three specially equipped cabs to exchange their car's depleted battery pack for a 100 miles (160km) fully recharged one in 59.1 seconds on average.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Better Place used the same technology to swap batteries that
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F-16" title="F-16">
       F-16
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Jet_aircraft" title="Jet aircraft">
       jet
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Fighter_aircraft" title="Fighter aircraft">
       fighter aircraft
      </a>
      use to load their bombs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Better Place battery switch stations were claimed to support multiple battery types of all kinds of electric cars as long as the battery could be removed from under the car.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A battery switch station using only 15 batteries allegedly had the ability to swap batteries for 2,500 EV's.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Better Place claimed it had battery station installation teams who could install one battery switch station in just two days,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      one every 25 miles in every route
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and at the same cost of 7 days of oil in the United States, Better Place claimed it could cover all of the United States with battery switch stations and all the required infrastructure.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Battery_switching_versus_DC_fast_charging">
       Battery switching versus DC fast charging
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Battery switching versus DC fast charging">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The main alternative technology to the battery-switching technique promoted by Better Place is DC fast charging. A nationwide fast charging infrastructure is/was being deployed in the United States that by 2013 would cover the entire nation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      DC Fast Chargers are going to be installed at 45
      <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">
       BP
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/ARCO" title="ARCO">
       ARCO
      </a>
      locations and will be made available to the public as early as March 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Better Place claimed that its
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subscription" title="Subscription">
       subscription
      </a>
      model had customers effectively paying only the prorated mileage cost without any battery ownership problems, whereas the fast charging model involves the customer bearing all the battery purchase, ownership, maintenance, and replacement costs, in addition to the cost of the electricity to recharge the battery.
     </p>
     <p>
      Better Place claimed that far fewer fast charging and battery switch stations would be needed than the current number of petroleum fuel refill stations, because drivers would usually recharge ("refuel") electric cars at home, offices, shopping centers, commercial areas, and the like. Drivers would only need alternatives if they forgot to recharge, couldn't get to a charge spot, had insufficient time at a charge spot, or were driving non-stop in excess of 160-kilometre (99mi), typical of long distance vacations and business trips.
     </p>
     <p>
      DC fast charging was at the time considerably slower than Better Place's claimed 59 second battery switchover, but while Better Place battery switch stations would have cost around $500,000 each, DC fast chargers that the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EV_Project" title="EV Project">
       EV project
      </a>
      is/was to deploy would cost only between $25,000 to $40,000.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wheels.blogs.nytimes.com_78-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-wheels.blogs.nytimes.com-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Demonstration_projects">
       Demonstration projects
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Demonstration projects">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Yokohama">
       Yokohama
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Yokohama">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      On May 13, 2009, Better Place premiered their battery switching station to the public in
      <a href="/wiki/Yokohama" title="Yokohama">
       Yokohama
      </a>
      where BP had been invited by the Japanese Ministry of the Environment.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The battery switching station demonstrated was set up similarly to a gas station automatic car wash. The vehicle drove up on a ramp and was aligned on the swapping pad. The battery shuttle then engaged and rose up toward the bottom of the vehicle. It made contact with the battery, released it, lowered it, and moved the depleted battery pack away from the car. The charged battery pack was then inserted. The discharged battery was returned to the charging bay. The battery switch was complete in less than two minutes and the vehicle drove away.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The battery swap was designed to require less time than filling a tank of gas.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Agassi_TED_talk_39-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Agassi_TED_talk-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In order to keep electric vehicles in demand, Better Place was going to try to keep the vehicles competitive with the other cars on the market. By building infrastructure that made owning an electric car more practical, they hoped to increase demand.
     </p>
     <p>
      The first prototype battery switch station opened in Yokohama, Japan on May 14, 2009, was designed by Yoav Heichal, chief engineer for Better Place research and development group.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The company signed an agreement with Dor Alon Energy to install battery replacement points, which would run alongside the petroleum refueling station' normal business. Dor Alon CEO, Israel Yaniv, said, "Dor Alon is the first energy company that will enable owners of electric car owners of the future to obtain electric refueling services at its gas stations. We consider this agreement with Better Place to be a strategic partnership that will create real value and innovation for the company's activity."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Tokyo">
       Tokyo
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Tokyo">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      On April 2010, a 90-day switchable-battery electric taxi demonstration project was launched in
      <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">
       Tokyo
      </a>
      , using three
      <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Rogue" title="Nissan Rogue">
       Nissan Rogue
      </a>
      crossover utility vehicles, converted into
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">
       electric cars
      </a>
      with switchable batteries provided by
      <a href="/wiki/A123_Systems" title="A123 Systems">
       A123 Systems
      </a>
      . The battery switch station deployed in Tokyo was more advanced than the Yokohama switch system demonstrated in 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During the three-month field test the EV taxis accumulated over 25,000 miles (40,000km) and swapped batteries 2,122 times, with an average battery swap time of 59.1 seconds. Nissan decided to continue the trial until late November 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="San_Francisco">
       San Francisco
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: San Francisco">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      In October 2010 Better Place announced its commitment to launch a three-year demonstration program with electric-powered taxis in the
      <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">
       San Francisco Bay Area
      </a>
      , in partnership with the cities of
      <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">
       San Francisco
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">
       San Jose, California
      </a>
      , taxi operators and
      <a href="/wiki/Carsharing" title="Carsharing">
       carsharing
      </a>
      programs, regional and state agencies, consumer and EV organizations, and the
      <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Public_Utilities_Commission" title="San Francisco Public Utilities Commission">
       San Francisco Public Utilities Commission
      </a>
      . The program would deploy and operate four battery switching stations in the San Francisco to San Jose corridor to support a fleet of switchable-battery EV taxis.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC1010_89-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-GCC1010-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of December 2011
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , Better Place had made no further statements of progress on this program.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">
       Netherlands
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Netherlands">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      A battery-powered 10-taxi demonstration project was launched at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schiphol_Airport" title="Schiphol Airport">
       Schiphol Airport
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">
       Amsterdam
      </a>
      in 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Investors">
       Investors
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Investors">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      As of 2010
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , the company had raised
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$700million
      </span>
      from various sources including,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VantagePoint_Venture_Partners" title="VantagePoint Venture Partners">
       VantagePoint Venture Partners
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Israel_Corporation" title="Israel Corporation">
       Israel Corporation
      </a>
      (33% ownership),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Israel_Cleantech_Ventures" title="Israel Cleantech Ventures">
       Israel Cleantech Ventures
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/HSBC" title="HSBC">
       HSBC
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">
       Morgan Stanley
      </a>
      , Acorns to Oaks II, Esarbee Investments Canada, GC Investments LLC, Musea Ventures,
      <a href="/wiki/Ofer_Brothers_Group" title="Ofer Brothers Group">
       Ofer Group
      </a>
      , Vyikra Partners, Wolfensohn &amp; Co. and Maniv Energy Capital.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HSBC_93-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HSBC-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In late 2007, Agassi began raising
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$111million
      </span>
      in Series-A funding for the project,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Better_PLC_SEC_Form-D_95-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Better_PLC_SEC_Form-D-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      one of the largest and fastest seed rounds in history.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Investors included
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VantagePoint_Venture_Partners" title="VantagePoint Venture Partners">
       VantagePoint Venture Partners
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Israel_Corporation" title="Israel Corporation">
       Israel Corporation
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Israel_Cleantech_Ventures" title="Israel Cleantech Ventures">
       Israel Cleantech Ventures
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">
       Morgan Stanley
      </a>
      , and private investors led by Michael Granoff of
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Maniv_Energy_Capital&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Maniv Energy Capital (page does not exist)">
       Maniv Energy Capital
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2009, the company raised an additional
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$135million
      </span>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2012)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      for Better Place Denmark, including an investment from DONG Energy the leading utility in Denmark. Following the announcement in Israel, Better Place said it had launched its network in Denmark, Australia and in two United States locations - Hawaii and Northern California. The company said it was in talks with more than 25 countries around the world.
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">
       Australia
      </a>
      , Better Place announced agreements with AGL Energy and financial advisor Macquarie Capital Group to raise
      <span style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a href="/wiki/Australian_dollar" title="Australian dollar">
        A$
       </a>
       1billion
      </span>
      and begin deploying an electric vehicle (EV) network powered by renewable energy. According to Better Place, its model for sustainable mobility would help Australia move toward oil independence. With the worlds seventh highest per capita rate of car ownership, the country had nearly 15 million cars on the road after adding over a million new cars in 2007.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In January 2010, as Israel Corporation completed its investment of
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$100million
      </span>
      in the company,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      a consortium of investors signed a Series-B funding round to invest a further
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$350million
      </span>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in Better Place, citing their confidence that "Better Place has the technical and commercial solutions to allow for the mass adoption of electric cars in the near term." The Series-B round was led by
      <a href="/wiki/HSBC" title="HSBC">
       HSBC
      </a>
      , which invested
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$125million
      </span>
      , and included all Series-A investors plus
      <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">
       Morgan Stanley Investment Management
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Lazard#Asset_management" title="Lazard">
       Lazard Asset Management
      </a>
      . The deal represented one of the largest financial investments of its kind by HSBC, which gained a seat on the Better Place board of directors and approximately 10% of the company's shares.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HSBC_93-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HSBC-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      From its early days, doubts were raised as to the effectiveness of Better Place's centralised model of providing charging infrastructure, with some anticipating that the model would not be widely adopted.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Partners">
       Partners
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Partners">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In May 2008, the company presented a prototype of its electric car at a press conference in
      <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">
       Tel Aviv
      </a>
      . Shai Agassi estimated that the company's partner, the Renault-Nissan alliance, would likely invest $500 million to $1 billion in developing the swappable-battery electric cars.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Further partnerships with other manufacturers were not announced, and Peter Rawlinson, VP and Chief Engineer for Vehicle Engineering at Tesla was quoted as saying Different batteries suit different cars. Its far too simplistic to look at batteries as isolation,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Better Place also announced plans to develop electric recharge grids in the city of
      <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">
       San Francisco
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the state of
      <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">
       Hawaii
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Australian finance group
      <a href="/wiki/Macquarie_Group" title="Macquarie Group">
       Macquarie
      </a>
      said it would work with Better Place to fund the construction of plug-in stations, and Australian utility
      <a href="/wiki/AGL_Energy" title="AGL Energy">
       AGL Energy
      </a>
      committed to powering those stations with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renewable_electricity" title="Renewable electricity">
       renewable electricity
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        105
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Response">
       Response
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Response">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      In March 2008,
      <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">
       Deutsche Bank
      </a>
      analysts issued a glowing report on the company stating that its approach could be a "paradigm shift" that caused "massive disruption" to the auto industry, and which had "the potential to eliminate the gasoline engine altogether."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Three months later, the same institution issued a second report, finding "electric vehicles destined for much more growth than is widely perceived". The same report stated that "[i]mprovements in battery technology will allow for increased power, increased electrical propulsion, and bigger gains in fuel economy."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On June 26, 2008, Shai Agassi testified before the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">
       United States House of Representatives
      </a>
      Select Committee on Energy Independence and Global Warming. The hearing, titled "$4 Gasoline and Fuel Economy: Auto Industry at a Crossroads," dealt with the future role of the auto industry and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_federal_government" title="United States federal government">
       federal government
      </a>
      in fighting gas prices and the fuel economy standards proposed in response to the enactment of the
      <a href="/wiki/Energy_Independence_and_Security_Act_of_2007" title="Energy Independence and Security Act of 2007">
       Energy Independence and Security Act (EISA) of 2007
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2009, CBS Money Watch cast doubts on Better Place's business model, noting that it would cost up to $500,000 to construct a charging station
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-station500k_66-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-station500k-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Markets_and_pricing">
       Markets and pricing
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Markets and pricing">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">
       Australia
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
