       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Australia">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Better_Place_Australia_car_Stevage.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Better_Place_Australia_car_Stevage.jpg/220px-Better_Place_Australia_car_Stevage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Better_Place_Australia_car_Stevage.jpg/330px-Better_Place_Australia_car_Stevage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Better_Place_Australia_car_Stevage.jpg/440px-Better_Place_Australia_car_Stevage.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Better_Place_Australia_car_Stevage.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A Better Place
        <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_i-MiEV" title="Mitsubishi i-MiEV">
         Mitsubishi i-MiEV
        </a>
        company car in Melbourne.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EV_recharge_spot_at_Belconnen_Markets_February_2015.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3351" data-file-width="4465" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/EV_recharge_spot_at_Belconnen_Markets_February_2015.jpg/220px-EV_recharge_spot_at_Belconnen_Markets_February_2015.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/EV_recharge_spot_at_Belconnen_Markets_February_2015.jpg/330px-EV_recharge_spot_at_Belconnen_Markets_February_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/EV_recharge_spot_at_Belconnen_Markets_February_2015.jpg/440px-EV_recharge_spot_at_Belconnen_Markets_February_2015.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EV_recharge_spot_at_Belconnen_Markets_February_2015.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A public Better Place charging station in Canberra.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In Australia a roll out of 500 charge stations was planned to begin in the major eastern coast cities before expanding nationally. It was estimated that these would give comparable coverage to the existing 13,000 petrol stations then in operation.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      The total cost of this roll out was claimed to be between $1 to $1.25 billion AUD.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
       <a href="#cite_note-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The first charge spot was installed in
      <a href="/wiki/Canberra" title="Canberra">
       Canberra
      </a>
      in late 2011,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC1010_89-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-GCC1010-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but in January 2013, after fewer than 20 public charge spots had been installed
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
       <a href="#cite_note-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the rollout was halted and the board of Better Place decided to concentrate on its two existing markets, Israel and Denmark.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Austonhold_25-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Austonhold-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Better Place was also to be the preferred provider of home and dealership charging stations for the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holden_Volt" title="Holden Volt">
       Holden Volt
      </a>
      , with the partnership announced in July 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="China">
       China
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: China">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 2011, Better Place announced an agreement with
      <a href="/wiki/China_Southern_Power_Grid_Company" title="China Southern Power Grid Company">
       China Southern Power Grid Company
      </a>
      , the worlds eighth-largest utility company. Before the end of the year, Better Place was going to open a battery switch station and joint education center in the southern city of Guangzhou. Shai Agassi said that China Southern Grid was embracing battery switch as the primary means of range extension.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
       <a href="#cite_note-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
       <a href="#cite_note-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      China Southern Grid Chairman Zhao Jianguo said that the battery-switch model might become mainstream in China and that the joint visitor center and battery switch demonstration project with Better Place would help promote electric-car adoption in China by allowing potential customers to experience this innovative solution.
     </p>
     <p>
      China Southern Power Grid pilot projects and other joint activities were supposed to explore the benefits that switchable-battery electric cars and the networked infrastructure that supports them might deliver to the electric grid in CSG's service area, which spanned five provinces, one million square kilometers, and 230 million people in Southern China.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Better_Place.2C_China_Southern_Grid_Sign_Strategic_Agreement_Centered_on_Battery_Switch_Model_115-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Better_Place.2C_China_Southern_Grid_Sign_Strategic_Agreement_Centered_on_Battery_Switch_Model-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Electric utility
      <a href="/wiki/State_Grid_Corporation_of_China" title="State Grid Corporation of China">
       State Grid Corporation of China
      </a>
      planned to build over 2,351 electric-charging and battery-swap stations by 2016. These would have had 220,000
      <a href="/wiki/Charging_station" title="Charging station">
       charging poles
      </a>
      , but they did not indicate how many, if any, of them would have been battery-swap stations. The director of the State Grid smart grid research center commented "The construction of a large-scale charging station costs 20 to 30 million yuan ($3.05-4.57 million) and a small-scale one costs less than 10 million yuan, but it costs more than 100 million yuan to build a battery-swap station."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_Grid_2011_plans_116-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-State_Grid_2011_plans-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In April 2010, Better Place signed a
      <a href="/wiki/Memorandum_of_understanding" title="Memorandum of understanding">
       memorandum of understanding
      </a>
      with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chery_Automobile" title="Chery Automobile">
       Chery Automobile
      </a>
      , China's biggest independent car maker, to develop prototypes for electric vehicles to be used in regional state-sponsored pilot projects.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Better_Place_and_Chery_announce_agreement_to_collaborate_on_electric_vehicle_technology_117-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Better_Place_and_Chery_announce_agreement_to_collaborate_on_electric_vehicle_technology-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Denmark">
       Denmark
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Denmark">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Renault_Fluence_Z.E._%E2%80%93_Frontansicht,_11._Februar_2013,_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1595" data-file-width="3402" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Renault_Fluence_Z.E._%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_11._Februar_2013%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/220px-Renault_Fluence_Z.E._%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_11._Februar_2013%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Renault_Fluence_Z.E._%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_11._Februar_2013%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/330px-Renault_Fluence_Z.E._%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_11._Februar_2013%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Renault_Fluence_Z.E._%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_11._Februar_2013%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/440px-Renault_Fluence_Z.E._%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_11._Februar_2013%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Renault_Fluence_Z.E._%E2%80%93_Frontansicht,_11._Februar_2013,_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Renault_Fluence_Z.E." title="Renault Fluence Z.E.">
         Renault Fluence Z.E.
        </a>
        was the
        <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">
         electric car
        </a>
        available on the Better Place network in Israel and Denmark.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Batteriskiftestation_(better_place).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2880" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Batteriskiftestation_%28better_place%29.jpg/220px-Batteriskiftestation_%28better_place%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Batteriskiftestation_%28better_place%29.jpg/330px-Batteriskiftestation_%28better_place%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Batteriskiftestation_%28better_place%29.jpg/440px-Batteriskiftestation_%28better_place%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Batteriskiftestation_(better_place).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A Better Place battery swap station in Denmark.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Better Place partnered with Denmark's leading energy company;
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dong_Energy" title="Dong Energy">
       Dong Energy
      </a>
      , in a 103 million Euro (770 million Danish Kroner) investment to introduce electric cars and infrastructure to
      <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">
       Denmark
      </a>
      . The country currently generates 20% of its electric power from
      <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_Denmark" title="Wind power in Denmark">
       wind energy
      </a>
      , but much of it is exported because there is currently no way for utilities to store the excess power. Using the Better Place model, Dong hoped to take advantage of the existing electric grid and electric vehicle batteries to harness and store the abundance of wind-generated power, and distribute it appropriately for transportation consumption.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dong_Energy_Press_Release_118-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dong_Energy_Press_Release-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
       <a href="#cite_note-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Renault_Fluence_Z.E." title="Renault Fluence Z.E.">
       Renault Fluence Z.E.
      </a>
      sold in Denmark at a price of 205,000
      <a href="/wiki/Danish_krone" title="Danish krone">
       DKK
      </a>
      (27,496 or
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$38,378
      </span>
      ) including
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VAT" title="VAT">
       VAT
      </a>
      plus the monthly fee for the switchable-battery. Consumers paid a one-time fee of 9,995 DKK (1,341) for a private
      <a href="/wiki/Charging_station" title="Charging station">
       charging station
      </a>
      and customers were offered a choice of five fixed-price switchable-battery packages based on kilometers driven per year. For more than 40,000km (25,000mi) a year the monthly fee was 2,995 DKK (399) per month.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FZE3_120-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FZE3-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FZE2_121-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FZE2-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The network commercial launch was in late 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC1010_89-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-GCC1010-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The first
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battery_swapping" title="Battery swapping">
       battery switch station
      </a>
      in Denmark, out of 20 which were planned to be deployed across the country as part of the network of charging infrastructure, was unveiled in June 2011 at
      <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">
       <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Better_Place&amp;params=55_44_1.5_N_12_27_36_E_type:landmark_region:DK&amp;title=FirstChargingStationInDK">
        <span class="geo-default">
         <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
          <span class="latitude">
           55441.5N
          </span>
          <span class="longitude">
           122736E
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
        <span class="geo-multi-punct">
          / 
        </span>
        <span class="geo-nondefault">
         <span class="vcard">
          <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           55.733750N 12.46000E
          </span>
          <span style="display:none">
            /
           <span class="geo">
            55.733750; 12.46000
           </span>
          </span>
          <span style="display:none">
            (
           <span class="fn org">
            FirstChargingStationInDK
           </span>
           )
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </a>
      </span>
      in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gladsaxe" title="Gladsaxe">
       Gladsaxe
      </a>
      , near
      <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">
       Copenhagen
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC0611_68-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-GCC0611-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Sales of the Fluence Z.E. began in late 2011, and 198 units were sold in Denmark through December 2012. Cumulative sales through April 2013 reached 234 units.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denmark11_13_122-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Denmark11_13-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of December 2012 there were 17 fully operational battery switch stations in the country, enabling Danish customers to drive anywhere across the country in an electric car.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Better_Place_Delivers_For_Demanding_Amsterdam_Taxi_Drivers_123-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Better_Place_Delivers_For_Demanding_Amsterdam_Taxi_Drivers-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 26 May 2013, and following the decision of the Board of Directors of Better Place's global company, Better Place Danmark A/S decided to begin
      <a href="/wiki/Bankruptcy" title="Bankruptcy">
       bankruptcy
      </a>
      proceedings. Because the batteries are owned by Better Place, Renault announced it would honor the existing agreement to around 500 customers that bought their electric cars through Better Place.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPDenmark01_27-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-BPDenmark01-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPDenmark02_28-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-BPDenmark02-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Hawaii">
       Hawaii
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Hawaii">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Better Place deployed about 80
      <a href="/wiki/Charging_station" title="Charging station">
       charging stations
      </a>
      and 154 charge points in
      <a href="/wiki/Oahu" title="Oahu">
       Oahu
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Maui" title="Maui">
       Maui
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kauai" title="Kauai">
       Kauai
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_(island)" title="Hawaii (island)">
       Big Island
      </a>
      , and had almost 700 customers. The operation of the charging stations were acquired in March 2013 by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OpConnect" title="OpConnect">
       OpConnect
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT053113_124-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT053113-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
       <a href="#cite_note-125">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        125
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      No interruption of service is expected due to Better Place bankruptcy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT053113_124-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT053113-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">
       Israel
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Israel">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BP_Renault_Fluence_ZE_Israel_Jan_2012.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="960" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/BP_Renault_Fluence_ZE_Israel_Jan_2012.jpg/220px-BP_Renault_Fluence_ZE_Israel_Jan_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/BP_Renault_Fluence_ZE_Israel_Jan_2012.jpg/330px-BP_Renault_Fluence_ZE_Israel_Jan_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/BP_Renault_Fluence_ZE_Israel_Jan_2012.jpg/440px-BP_Renault_Fluence_ZE_Israel_Jan_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BP_Renault_Fluence_ZE_Israel_Jan_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Parade of
        <a href="/wiki/Renault_Fluence_Z.E." title="Renault Fluence Z.E.">
         Renault Fluence Z.E.
        </a>
        electric cars enabled with battery swapping technology to commemorate the first deliveries to Better Place employees in Israel in January 2012.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RFZE01_126-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-RFZE01-126">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          126
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RFZE02_127-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-RFZE02-127">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          127
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bettr_place_car_1.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bettr_place_car_1.jpg/220px-Bettr_place_car_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bettr_place_car_1.jpg/330px-Bettr_place_car_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bettr_place_car_1.jpg/440px-Bettr_place_car_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bettr_place_car_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Renault_Fluence_Z.E." title="Renault Fluence Z.E.">
         Renault Fluence Z.E.
        </a>
        sold through Better Place in Israel.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parking,_Leonardo_Club_Hotel,_Tiberias_Tiberias_P1010812.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Parking%2C_Leonardo_Club_Hotel%2C_Tiberias_Tiberias_P1010812.JPG/220px-Parking%2C_Leonardo_Club_Hotel%2C_Tiberias_Tiberias_P1010812.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Parking%2C_Leonardo_Club_Hotel%2C_Tiberias_Tiberias_P1010812.JPG/330px-Parking%2C_Leonardo_Club_Hotel%2C_Tiberias_Tiberias_P1010812.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Parking%2C_Leonardo_Club_Hotel%2C_Tiberias_Tiberias_P1010812.JPG/440px-Parking%2C_Leonardo_Club_Hotel%2C_Tiberias_Tiberias_P1010812.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parking,_Leonardo_Club_Hotel,_Tiberias_Tiberias_P1010812.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Better Place charging stations outside the Leonardo Club Hotel in Tiberias.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
       Israel
      </a>
      was the first nation in the world to partner with Better Place to build an electric car infrastructure. Shai Agassi, former Better Place CEO, claimed that by 2016, plus or minus a year, more than 50% of cars sold in Israel would be electric.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        128
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Battery switch stations were supposedly opening to customers almost weekly in 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
       <a href="#cite_note-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      That map indicates with "orange circles" the handful of battery switch stations available in June 2012, and shows with "grey circles" the full buildout of battery switch stations expected by year's end. The Baran Group signed an agreement with Better Place stating its intention to build 51 battery switch stations over the course of 2011 to cover all of Israel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Jerusalem_Post_130-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Jerusalem_Post-130">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        130
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However progress was not nearly as rapid as was planned.
     </p>
     <p>
      According to the
      <a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">
       Financial Times
      </a>
      around 400 corporations in Israel signed letters of intent to begin switching their fleets to Better Place electric car network as soon as the service becomes available. This represented a potential of 80,000 electric cars.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Better_Place.E2.80.99s_.24200m_round_to_expand_electric_car_networks_131-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Better_Place.E2.80.99s_.24200m_round_to_expand_electric_car_networks-131">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        131
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Out of the 100,000
      <a href="/wiki/Renault_Fluence_Z.E." title="Renault Fluence Z.E.">
       Renault Fluence Z.E.
      </a>
      that Better Place agreed to buy from
      <a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">
       Renault
      </a>
      , the company claimed to have already signed around 70,000 orders, most of them from commercial fleet customers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Better_Place_CEO:_Biggest_obstacle_to_electric_cars_is_auto_industry_.27skepticism.27_132-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Better_Place_CEO:_Biggest_obstacle_to_electric_cars_is_auto_industry_.27skepticism.27-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Better Place launched its first battery-swapping station in Israel, in
      <a href="/wiki/Kiryat_Ekron" title="Kiryat Ekron">
       Kiryat Ekron
      </a>
      , near
      <a href="/wiki/Rehovot" title="Rehovot">
       Rehovot
      </a>
      in March 2011. The station was supposed to be the first of approximately 40 stations to begin operating in the near term. The battery exchange process took five minutes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JP240311_133-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-JP240311-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        133
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The company also erected over 1,000 functional charging spots for the cars and thousands more were supposed to be put in place by the end of 2011, according to the CEO of Better Place Israel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JP240311_133-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-JP240311-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        133
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Orders for the Renault Fluence ZE in Israel began in July 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Better_Place_unveils_Israeli_pricing_policy_134-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Better_Place_unveils_Israeli_pricing_policy-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        134
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to Better Place, their customers regular maintenance costs would be about 40% less than for regular family cars, insurance also will be less at around NIS 3,700 a year, and its comprehensive solution of electric car and services would cut annual vehicle maintenance costs by 20%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Better_Place_unveils_Israeli_pricing_policy_134-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Better_Place_unveils_Israeli_pricing_policy-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        134
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The first deliveries of the
      <a href="/wiki/Renault_Fluence_Z.E." title="Renault Fluence Z.E.">
       Renault Fluence Z.E.
      </a>
      took place on the 22nd of January 2012 and around 100 electric cars were allocated to Better Place's employees.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RFZE01_126-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-RFZE01-126">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        126
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RFZE02_127-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-RFZE02-127">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        127
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Better Place planned a staged delivery process as the infrastructure across the country was completed. Retail customer deliveries began in the second quarter of 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deliveries2012_2-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Deliveries2012-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of mid September 2012, there were 21 operational battery-swap stations open to the public in Israel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BWSet12_3-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-BWSet12-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cumulative sales through July 2012 reached 300 cars,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
       <a href="#cite_note-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and as of the end of October, just 490 cars had been sold, making the company's target of 4,000 customers by June 2013 a difficult goal to achieve.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SalesOct_136-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SalesOct-136">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        136
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In October 2012, Better Place signed a deal with Elco to supply 125 cars worth NIS 15m. The 125 Renault Fluence ZEs were to be delivered through 2012 and 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
       <a href="#cite_note-137">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        137
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of December 2012
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , a total of 518 cars were sold in the country. In the first four months of 2013, a total 422 cars were sold, bringing the total to 940.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SalesIsrael_138-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SalesIsrael-138">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        138
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
       <a href="#cite_note-139">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        139
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Alan Gelman, chief financial officer said in January 2013 that the company had turned a corner in recent weeks with large sales to fleets and that the days of not selling cars were over
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
       <a href="#cite_note-140">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        140
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nevertheless, on 26 May 2013 the company filed for bankruptcy in Israel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT052613_5-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT052613-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Electric_car_charging_spot_in_Israel.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Electric_car_charging_spot_in_Israel.JPG/220px-Electric_car_charging_spot_in_Israel.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Electric_car_charging_spot_in_Israel.JPG/330px-Electric_car_charging_spot_in_Israel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Electric_car_charging_spot_in_Israel.JPG/440px-Electric_car_charging_spot_in_Israel.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Electric_car_charging_spot_in_Israel.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Charging spot in Israel
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Customer_Qualifications">
       Customer Qualifications
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Customer Qualifications">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Better Place wanted electric car customers who could make a successful transition from
      <a href="/wiki/Range_anxiety" title="Range anxiety">
       range anxiety
      </a>
      to ordinary range awareness within the company's growing infrastructure. During the sales process, Better Place aimed to educate and assess each customer's electric car suitability. The company was going to exclude drivers frequently traveling irregular routes that span the country. Eventually, Israel was supposed to have enough battery switch stations and recharging spots at parking garages, shopping centers, hotels, commercial areas, and elsewhere, to cater for most drivers.
     </p>
     <p>
      At minimum, customers needed dedicated off-road parking at home and, for higher mileage drivers, Better Place was going to install charging spots at people's workplace. The preferred high-mileage customer might commute 130-kilometre (81mi) each way between home and office. Lower distance customers might only need their home charging spot, with battery switching being infrequent.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Israel_Electric_Grid">
       Israel Electric Grid
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Israel Electric Grid">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Electric cars aren't allowed by law to directly plug into ordinary Israeli electrical outlets. Better Place charging stations were to have
      <a href="/wiki/Smart_grid" title="Smart grid">
       smart grid
      </a>
      interactivity that automatically time shifted the charging process away from peak electrical demand hours. Most critics
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">
         <span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (May 2014)">
          who?
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      claimed it was an attempt to monopolize the charging of car batteries, and had in fact the reverse effect, and had discouraged many potential customers in Israel from buying Better Place's cars.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">
       Awards
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Awards">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Edmunds.com" title="Edmunds.com">
       Edmunds.com
      </a>
      selected battery-charging infrastructure developers
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coulomb_Technologies" title="Coulomb Technologies">
       Coulomb Technologies
      </a>
      and Better Place as recipients of its first annual
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Green_Car_Breakthrough_Award" title="Green Car Breakthrough Award">
       Green Car Breakthrough Award
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
       <a href="#cite_note-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2010, Shai Agassi was included at number 28 in a list of the 100 Top Global Thinkers published by Foreign Policy magazine, for his efforts to electric cars a mass-market success.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
       <a href="#cite_note-142">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        142
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Similar_projects">
       Similar projects
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Better_Place&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Similar projects">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_network" title="Electric vehicle network">
       Electric vehicle network
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      A number of companies have announced plans to install
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_network" title="Electric vehicle network">
       charging station networks
      </a>
      . In France,
      <a href="/wiki/%C3%89lectricit%C3%A9_de_France" title="lectricit de France">
       lectricit de France
      </a>
      (EDF) and
      <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">
       Toyota
      </a>
      announced plans to provide recharging points for PHEVs on roads, streets and
      <a href="/wiki/Parking_lot" title="Parking lot">
       parking lots
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
       <a href="#cite_note-143">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        143
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      EDF also announced a partnership with Elektromotive, Ltd.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
       <a href="#cite_note-144">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        144
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      to install 250 new charging points over six months from October 2007 in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London,_England" title="London, England">
       London
      </a>
      and elsewhere in the UK.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
       <a href="#cite_note-145">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        145
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coulomb_Technologies" title="Coulomb Technologies">
       Coulomb Technologies
      </a>
      was aiming to deploy its ChargePoint charging station network throughout the USA.
     </p>
     <p>
      In March 2009,
      <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Motors" title="Tesla Motors">
       Tesla Motors
      </a>
      announced a partnership to deploy
      <a href="/wiki/Tesla_station" title="Tesla station">
       battery swap stations
      </a>
      among their existing
      <i>
       Supercharger
      </i>
      network to service their
      <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_S" title="Tesla Model S">
       Model S
      </a>
      platform cars.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ramsey2009_146-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Ramsey2009-146">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        146
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
       <a href="#cite_note-147">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        147
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a class="external text" href="http://www.evchargermaps.com/" rel="nofollow">
       EV Charger Maps
      </a>
      project managed by
      <a class="external text" href="http://www.evchargernews.com/" rel="nofollow">
       EV Charger News
      </a>
      is a volunteer effort that manages a list of charging stations around the country with practical information targeted to electric vehicle owners. Recharging points also can be installed for specific uses, as in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taxi_stand" title="Taxi stand">
       taxi stands
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Nation-E" title="Nation-E">
       Nation-E
      </a>
      's Angel Car system is a portable unit containing a
      <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery" title="Lithium-ion battery">
       lithium-ion battery
      </a>
      that stores energy and is used as an emergency power charger for electric cars that run out of power. It designed to be a key solution to range anxiety in converting e-mobility into a reality without the deployments of significant new infrastructure, and provides fast charging services for all known Evs equipped with a fast-charging socket, including
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hybrid_car" title="Hybrid car">
       hybrid cars
      </a>
      , and it was also going to be available to charge Better Place's car, the
      <a href="/wiki/Renault_Fluence_Z.E." title="Renault Fluence Z.E.">
       Renault Fluence Z.E.
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-angel_car_148-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-angel_car-148">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        148
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

       <li id="cite_note-CBS_Morning_News-38">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-CBS_Morning_News_38-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation audio-visual">
          <a href="/wiki/Shai_Agassi" title="Shai Agassi">
           Shai Agassi
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/David_Pogue" title="David Pogue">
           David Pogue
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Gavin_Newsom" title="Gavin Newsom">
           Gavin Newsom
          </a>
          (2009-03-19).
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mXfqGL3C2uI" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            Making The World A 'Better Place'
           </i>
          </a>
          (YouTube). San Francisco, CA: CBS News Sunday Morning; CBS Interactive, Inc. Event occurs at 3:45.
          <q>
           Shai Agassi: "We [Better Place] don't let you [the customer] buy a battery; we [Better Place] buy the battery.
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABetter+Place&amp;rft.btitle=Making+The+World+A+%27Better+Place%27&amp;rft.date=2009-03-19&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.youtube.com%2Fwatch%3Fv%3DmXfqGL3C2uI&amp;rft.place=San+Francisco%2C+CA&amp;rft.pub=CBS+News+Sunday+Morning%3B+CBS+Interactive%2C+Inc&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-Agassi_TED_talk-39">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         ^
         <a href="#cite_ref-Agassi_TED_talk_39-0">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             a
            </b>
           </i>
          </sup>
         </a>
         <a href="#cite_ref-Agassi_TED_talk_39-1">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             b
            </b>
           </i>
          </sup>
         </a>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation audio-visual">
          Shai Agassi (February 2009).
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.ted.com/talks/shai_agassi_on_electric_cars.html" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            Shai Agassi's bold plan for electric cars
           </i>
          </a>
          . Long Beach and Palm Springs, California:
          <a href="/wiki/TED_(conference)" title="TED (conference)">
           TED
          </a>
          . Event occurs at 4m10s
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            2009-10-05
           </span>
          </span>
          .
          <q>
           See we're bound by today's technology on batteries, which is about 120 miles if you want to stay within reasonable space and weight limitations. 120 miles is a good enough range for a lot of people. But you never want to get stuck. So what we added as a second element to our network is a battery swap system. You drive. You take your depleted battery out. A full battery comes on. And you drive on. You don't do it as a human being. You do it as a machine. It looks like a car wash. You come into your car wash. And a plate comes up, holds your battery, takes it out, puts it back in. Within two minutes you're back on the road. And you can go again. If you had charge spots everywhere, and you had battery swap stations everywhere, how often would you do it? And it ends up that you'd do swapping less times than you stop at a gas station. As a matter of fact, we add it to the contract. We said that if you stop to swap your battery more than 50 times a year we start paying you money because it's an inconvenience.
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABetter+Place&amp;rft.btitle=Shai+Agassi%27s+bold+plan+for+electric+cars&amp;rft.date=February+2009&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ted.com%2Ftalks%2Fshai_agassi_on_electric_cars.html&amp;rft.place=Long+Beach+and+Palm+Springs%2C+California&amp;rft.pub=TED&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>

       <li id="cite_note-Agassi_CNBC-42">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-Agassi_CNBC_42-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation audio-visual">
          <a href="/wiki/Shai_Agassi" title="Shai Agassi">
           Shai Agassi
          </a>
          , Amanda Drury, Martin Soong (2009-04-23).
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnbc.com/id/15840232?video=1102194519&amp;play=1" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            A Better Place for the Auto Industry
           </i>
          </a>
          (Flash video). CNBC Squawk Box. Event occurs at 2m40s
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            2009-10-10
           </span>
          </span>
          .
         </span>
        </span>
        <div style="clear:both;">
        </div>
        <q>
         2m40s: CNBC's Amanda Drury: "Are you going to have a monopoly on this infrastructure? How are you
        </q>
        <p>
         <q>
          going to make sure there is enough competition in the system to be able to maintain, you know, good
         </q>
        </p>
        <q>
         pricing, stable pricing for the consumer?"
        </q>
        <div style="clear:both;">
        </div>
        <p>
         <q>
          2m58s: Shai Agassi: ... in every country we come in, we've asked [the government] to force everybody, including ourselves [Better Place], to use international standards. And we've guaranteed, and asked for the same thing, that there will be open access for people to charge on our network even if they're not our subscribers. Sort of free roaming across networks so that there is an incentive for a second and third and fourth maker of ... sort of At&amp;T and Vodafone and Orange ... to actually go ahead and build networks that are compatible and based on standards.
         </q>

          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </p>

       <li id="cite_note-Agassi.2C_Dec_28_2008-60">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-Agassi.2C_Dec_28_2008_60-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation audio-visual">
          <a href="/wiki/Shai_Agassi" title="Shai Agassi">
           Shai Agassi
          </a>
          , Better Place, CEO, Founder; Chris Anderson,
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wired_Magazine" title="Wired Magazine">
           Wired Magazine
          </a>
          ,
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Editor-in-Chief" title="Editor-in-Chief">
           Editor-in-Chief
          </a>
          (2008-12-28).
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gNIijgJcsbs" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            Agassi's Electric Car Grid
           </i>
          </a>
          <span style="font-size:85%;">
           (ADOBE FLASH VIDEO)
          </span>
          (Videotape). Event occurs at 11m08s.
         </span>
        </span>
        <div style="clear:both;">
        </div>
        <q>
         Agassi, 11m08s: The battery costs are, gets you to, about 4 to 5 cents a mile when you take the entire life of the battery and electrons [electricity] cost you between 1 to 2 cents per mile.
        </q>
        <div style="clear:both;">
        </div>
        <q>
         Anderson, 11m29s: Does this include the subsidy for the car?
        </q>
        <div style="clear:both;">
        </div>
        <q>
         Agassi, 11m31s: Including nothing, base; no-taxes, no-subsidies, no-give aways. 4 to 5 cents a mile for the battery, 1 or 2 cents a mile for the electricity depending on whether you use coal or, you do what we [Better Place] do, you use wind and solar at 2 cents. So we're roughly at about 6, 7 cents a mile.
        </q>
        <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABetter+Place&amp;rft.btitle=Agassi%27s+Electric+Car+Grid&amp;rft.date=2008-12-28&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.youtube.com%2Fwatch%3Fv%3DgNIijgJcsbs&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">

         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABetter+Place&amp;rft.au=De+Danske+Bilimport%C3%B8rer&amp;rft.aulast=De+Danske+Bilimport%C3%B8rer&amp;rft.btitle=Statistik+-+Nyregistreringstal+-+Personbiler+-+Pr.model%3A+2012+-Hele+%C3%A5ret+%26++Pr.model%3A+januar+-+april+2013&amp;rft.date=May+2013&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.bilimp.dk%2Fstatistics%2Findex.asp&amp;rft.pub=Bilimp&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         <i>
          Select year and click on Pr. model for details of sales by brand and model.
         </i>
         <i>
          198 units were sold in 2012 and 36 through March 2013
         </i>
         .
